FREQUENCY ANALYSIS OF METEOROLOGICAL DATA MEASURED AT
  Dhaka city

Station latitude:   23.2222
Station longitude:   90.2222
Station height above mean sea level:   10 metres.

Period of analysis:  1/ 1/1981 to 31/12/1990.

Effective height of anemometer above ground level:  20 metres.
Roughness length assumed at station:  0.200 metres.
          Parameter and units                             No. of classes
     Hourly average wind speed (m/s) (=U)                     5
     Hourly average wind direction (degrees true) (=PHI)     12
     Surface sensible heat flux (W/m**2) (=FTHETA0)           7
     Boundary layer depth (m) (=H)                            7
     Hourly rainfall amount (mm) (=P)                         3

The surface albedo is: 0.23

This analysis gives the frequencies with which the above parameters fall
within particular classes. The upper limits of the classes are as follows:

U-class upper limits in knots:
     3     6    10    16 32767
PHI-class upper limits in degrees:
    15    45    75   105   135   165   195   225   255   285   315   345
FTHETA0-class upper limits in W/m**2:
   -30   -10     0    50   100   150 32767
H-class upper limits in m:
   100   200   300   500   800  1200 32767
P-class upper limits in tenths of mm:
     0     6 32767
Values equal to the upper limit of a particular class lie within that
class. The hourly average wind direction is cyclic (i.e. the first class
includes those values which exceed the last upper limit).

1m/s = 1.942 knots.

Note the rainfall classes are defined in tenths of mm, but the results
are presented in mm. tenths of mm (=mm/10).

Occasions when the wind speed is calm or the direction is variable are
not included in the analysis. The total number of such hours is   2245.
The number of such hours occurring in periods restricted by month and/or
hour are as follows:

A positive sensible heat flux means heat is flowing from the atmosphere to the surface, 
A negative sensible heat flux means heat is flowing from the surface to the atmosphere.

This analysis is formatted to be easily used as input to UK-ADMS. The
data given below is presented in the form of a single record for each
combination of parameter classes. Each record contains the following
information:
   1. Average of U for occasions when U falls in the particular U-class
   2. Value of PHI at the mid point of the particular PHI-class
   3. Average of FTHETA0 for occasions when FTHETA0 falls in the particular
      FTHETA0-class
   4. Average of H for occasions when H falls in the particular H-class
   5. Average of P for occasions when P falls in the particular
      P-class
   6. Number of occasions when U, PHI, FTHETA0, H and P fall
      simultaneously (FH) within the particular U-, PHI-, FTHETA0-, H- and
      P-classes
   7 to 30. Number of occasions when U, PHI, FTHETA0, H and P fall
      simultaneously within the particular U-, PHI-, FTHETA0-, H- and
      P-classes in periods restricted by month and/or hour as
      follows:
      Months 12 to  2, hours 22 to  5 (inclusive)
      Months 12 to  2, hours  6 to  9 (inclusive)
      Months 12 to  2, hours 10 to 12 (inclusive)
      Months 12 to  2, hours 13 to 15 (inclusive)
      Months 12 to  2, hours 16 to 18 (inclusive)
      Months 12 to  2, hours 19 to 21 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours 22 to  5 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours  6 to  9 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours 10 to 12 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours 13 to 15 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours 16 to 18 (inclusive)
      Months  3 to  5, hours 19 to 21 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours 22 to  5 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours  6 to  9 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours 10 to 12 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours 13 to 15 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours 16 to 18 (inclusive)
      Months  6 to  8, hours 19 to 21 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours 22 to  5 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours  6 to  9 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours 10 to 12 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours 13 to 15 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours 16 to 18 (inclusive)
      Months  9 to 11, hours 19 to 21 (inclusive)
To save space, no record is given for those combinations of classes which
do not occur.

In the above, FR is short for frequency. The line FR instructs
UK-ADMS to take the 6th number in each record as the frequency with
which the particular combination of classes occurs. The parameters names
after FR are not recognised by UK-ADMS. However, by changing the
above lines in the obvious way, UK-ADMS can be instructed to take the 7th
or subsequent number as the frequency. In this way UK-ADMS can be made
to use frequency data restricted to certain months of the year and/or
times of day.

The remaining lines give the frequencies in the format described above.
